<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Irrigation1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="597" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Irrigation1.jpg/220px-Irrigation1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Irrigation1.jpg/330px-Irrigation1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Irrigation1.jpg/440px-Irrigation1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Irrigation1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Increased use of irrigation played a major role in the green revolution.</div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Biodiversity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The spread of Green Revolution agriculture affected both agricultural <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a> (or agrodiversity) and wild biodiversity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rice-robbery_90-1"><a href="#cite_note-rice-robbery-90">[90]</a></sup> There is little disagreement that the Green Revolution acted to reduce agricultural biodiversity, as it relied on just a few high-yield varieties of each crop.
</p><p>This has led to concerns about the susceptibility of a food supply to pathogens that cannot be controlled by agrochemicals, as well as the permanent loss of many valuable genetic traits bred into traditional varieties over thousands of years. To address these concerns, massive seed banks such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Consultative_Group_on_International_Agricultural_Research" title="Consultative Group on International Agricultural Research">Consultative Group on International Agricultural Research</a>’s (CGIAR) International Plant Genetic Resources Institute (now <a href="/wiki/Bioversity_International" title="Bioversity International">Bioversity International</a>) have been established (see <a href="/wiki/Svalbard_Global_Seed_Vault" title="Svalbard Global Seed Vault">Svalbard Global Seed Vault</a>).
</p><p>There are varying opinions about the effect of the Green Revolution on wild biodiversity. One hypothesis speculates that by increasing production per unit of land area, agriculture will not need to expand into new, uncultivated areas to feed a growing human population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Davies2003_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-Davies2003-95">[95]</a></sup> However, <a href="/wiki/Land_degradation" title="Land degradation">land degradation</a> and soil nutrients depletion have forced farmers to clear  forested areas in order to maintain production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Shiva1991_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-Shiva1991-96">[96]</a></sup> A counter-hypothesis speculates that biodiversity was sacrificed because traditional systems of agriculture that were displaced sometimes incorporated practices to preserve wild biodiversity, and because the Green Revolution expanded agricultural development into new areas where it was once unprofitable or too arid. For example, the development of wheat varieties tolerant to acid soil conditions with high aluminium content permitted the introduction of agriculture in sensitive <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Brazil" title="Wildlife of Brazil">Brazilian ecosystems</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Cerrado" title="Cerrado">Cerrado</a> <a href="/wiki/Tropical_savanna_climate" title="Tropical savanna climate">semi-humid</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_savanna" title="Tropical savanna">tropical savanna</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amazon_rainforest" title="Amazon rainforest">Amazon rainforest</a> in the geoeconomic macroregions of <a href="/wiki/Brazil_socio-geographic_division" title="Brazil socio-geographic division">Centro-Sul and Amazônia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Davies2003_95-1"><a href="#cite_note-Davies2003-95">[95]</a></sup> Before the Green Revolution, other Brazilian ecosystems were also significantly damaged by human activity, such as the once 1st or 2nd main contributor to Brazilian megadiversity <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mata_Atl%C3%A2ntica" title="Mata Atlântica">Atlantic Rainforest</a> (above 85% of deforestation in the 1980s, about 95% after the 2010s) and the important <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Xeric_shrubland" title="Xeric shrubland">xeric shrublands</a> called <a href="/wiki/Caatinga" title="Caatinga">Caatinga</a> mainly in <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Region,_Brazil" title="Northeast Region, Brazil">Northeastern Brazil</a> (about 40% in the 1980s, about 50% after the 2010s – deforestation of the Caatinga biome is generally associated with greater risks of <a href="/wiki/Desertification" title="Desertification">desertification</a>). This also caused many animal species to suffer due to their damaged habitats.
</p><p>Nevertheless, the world community has clearly acknowledged the negative aspects of <a href="/wiki/Agricultural_expansion" title="Agricultural expansion">agricultural expansion</a> as the 1992 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rio_Treaty" title="Rio Treaty">Rio Treaty</a>, signed by 189 nations, has generated numerous national <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biodiversity_Action_Plans" title="Biodiversity Action Plans">Biodiversity Action Plans</a> which assign significant <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_loss" title="Biodiversity loss">biodiversity loss</a> to agriculture's expansion into new domains.
</p><p>The Green Revolution has been criticized for an agricultural model which relied on a few staple and market profitable crops, and pursuing a model which limited the biodiversity of Mexico. One of the critics against these techniques  and the Green Revolution as a whole was <a href="/wiki/Carl_O._Sauer" title="Carl O. Sauer">Carl O. Sauer</a>, a geography professor at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Berkeley" title="University of California, Berkeley">University of California, Berkeley</a>. According to Sauer these techniques of plant breeding would result in negative effects on the country's resources, and the culture:
</p>
<blockquote>
<p>"A good aggressive bunch of American agronomists and plant breeders could ruin the native resources for good and all by pushing their American commercial stocks... And Mexican agriculture cannot be pointed toward standardization on a few commercial types without upsetting native economy and culture hopelessly... Unless the Americans understand that, they'd better keep out of this country entirely. That must be approached from an appreciation of native economies as being basically sound".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup>
</p>
</blockquote>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Greenhouse_gas_emissions">Greenhouse gas emissions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Greenhouse gas emissions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Studies indicate that the Green Revolution has substantially reduced emissions of the greenhouse gas CO<sub style="font-size: 80%;vertical-align: -0.35em">2</sub>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup>  According to a study published in 2013 in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PNAS" title="PNAS">PNAS</a>, in the absence of the crop germplasm improvement associated with the Green Revolution, <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas_emissions" title="Greenhouse gas emissions">greenhouse gas emissions</a> would have been 5.2–7.4 Gt higher than observed in 1965–2004.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-:5-11">[11]</a></sup> High yield agriculture has dramatic effects on the amount of carbon cycling in the atmosphere. The way in which farms are grown, in tandem with the seasonal carbon cycling of various crops, could alter the impact carbon in the atmosphere has on global warming. Wheat, rice, and soybean crops account for a significant amount of the increase in carbon in the atmosphere over the last 50 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup>
</p><p>Poorly regulated applications of nitrogen fertilizer that exceed the amount used by plants, such as broadcast applications of <a href="/wiki/Urea" title="Urea">urea</a>, results in emissions of <a href="/wiki/Nitrous_oxide" title="Nitrous oxide">nitrous oxide</a>, a potent greenhouse gas, and in water pollution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WP122221_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-WP122221-100">[100]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Dependence_on_non-renewable_resources">Dependence on non-renewable resources</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Dependence on non-renewable resources">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Most high intensity agricultural production is highly reliant on agricultural machinery and transport, as well as the production of pesticides and nitrates that all require energy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fertilizer#Nitrogen_fertilizers" title="Fertilizer">Nitrogen fertilizer</a> is a direct fossil fuel product processed primarily from <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a>. It is estimated that no more than 3.7 billion people of the current <a href="/wiki/World_population" title="World population">world population</a> could be fed without this single fossil fuel agricultural input.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> Moreover, the essential mineral nutrient phosphorus is often a limiting factor in crop cultivation, while phosphorus mines are rapidly being depleted worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Land_use">Land use</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Land use">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>A 2021 study found that the Green Revolution led to a reduction in land used for agriculture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_8-5"><a href="#cite_note-:1-8">[8]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_impact">Health impact</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Health impact">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Studies have found that the Green Revolution substantially reduced infant mortality in the developing world. A 2020 study of 37 developing countries found that the diffusion of modern crop varieties "reduced infant mortality by 2.4–5.3 percentage points (from a baseline of 18%), with stronger effects for male infants and among poor households."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-:3-9">[9]</a></sup> Another 2020 study found that high yield crop varieties reduced infant mortality in India, with particularly large effects for rural children, boys and low-caste children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-:4-10">[10]</a></sup>
</p><p>Consumption of <a href="/wiki/Health_effects_of_pesticides" title="Health effects of pesticides">pesticides</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fertilizer" title="Fertilizer">fertilizer agrochemicals</a> associated with the Green Revolution may have adverse health impacts. For example, pesticides may increase the likelihood of cancer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Loyn_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-Loyn-104">[104]</a></sup> Poor farming practices including non-compliance to usage of masks and over-usage of the chemicals compound this situation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Loyn_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-Loyn-104">[104]</a></sup> In 1989, WHO and UNEP estimated that there were around 1 million human pesticide poisonings annually. Some 20,000 (mostly in developing countries) ended in death, as a result of poor labeling, loose safety standards etc.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> A 2014 study found that Indian children who were exposed to higher quantities of fertilizer agrochemicals experienced more adverse health impacts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Punjab_case">Punjab case</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Punjab case">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Green_Revolution_in_India" title="Green Revolution in India">Green Revolution in India</a></div>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Greenpeace" title="Greenpeace">Greenpeace</a> Research Laboratories investigation of 50 villages in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muktsar" title="Muktsar">Muktsar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bathinda" title="Bathinda">Bathinda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ludhiana_district" title="Ludhiana district">Ludhiana districts</a> revealed that twenty percent of the sampled wells had nitrate levels above WHO limits for drinking water. The 2009 study linked the nitrate pollution with high use of synthetic nitrogen <a href="/wiki/Fertilizer" title="Fertilizer">fertilizers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span id="Norman_Borlaug.27s_response_to_criticism"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Norman_Borlaug's_response_to_criticism">Norman Borlaug's response to criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Norman Borlaug's response to criticism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Borlaug dismissed certain claims of critics, but also cautioned, "There are no miracles in agricultural production. Nor is there such a thing as a miracle variety of wheat, rice, or maize which can serve as an elixir to cure all ills of a stagnant, traditional agriculture."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup>
</p><p>Of environmental lobbyists, he said:
</p>
<blockquote><p>some of the environmental lobbyists of the Western nations are the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salt_and_Light#Cultural_references" title="Salt and Light">salt of the earth</a>, but many of them are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elitist" title="Elitist">elitists</a>. They've never experienced the physical sensation of hunger. They do their lobbying from comfortable office suites in Washington or <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>...If they lived just one month amid the misery of the developing world, as I have for fifty years, they'd be crying out for tractors and fertilizer and irrigation canals and be outraged that fashionable elitists back home were trying to deny them these things.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_Green_Revolution">Second Green Revolution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Second Green Revolution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Second_Green_Revolution" title="Second Green Revolution">Second Green Revolution</a></div>
<p>Although the Green Revolution has been able to improve agricultural output in some regions in the world, there was and is still room for improvement. As a result, many organizations continue to invent new ways to improve the techniques already used in the Green Revolution. Frequently quoted inventions are the <a href="/wiki/System_of_Rice_Intensification" title="System of Rice Intensification">System of Rice Intensification</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Marker-assisted_selection" title="Marker-assisted selection">marker-assisted selection</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Agroecology" title="Agroecology">agroecology</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> and applying existing technologies to agricultural problems of the developing world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> Current challenges for nations trying to modernize their agriculture include closing the urban-rural income gap, integration of smallholders into value chains, and maintaining competitiveness in the market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> However, in low-income countries, chronic problems such as poverty and hunger cause agricultural modernization efforts to be constrained.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> It is projected that global populations by 2050 will increase by one-third and as such will require a 70% increase in the production of food.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> Therefore, the Second Green Revolution will likely focus on improving tolerances to pests and disease in addition to technological input use efficiency.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Evergreen_Revolution">Evergreen Revolution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Green_Revolution&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Evergreen Revolution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The term 'Evergreen Revolution'<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[a]</a></sup> was coined by Indian agricultural scientist <a href="/wiki/M._S._Swaminathan" title="M. S. Swaminathan">M. S. Swaminathan</a> in 1990, though he has stated that the concept dates back to as early as 1968. It aims to represents an added dimension to the original concepts and practices of the green revolution, the ecological dimension.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:03_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-:03-118">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup> Swaminathan has described it as "productivity in perpetuity without associated ecological harm".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:03_118-1"><a href="#cite_note-:03-118">[117]</a></sup> The concept has evolved into a combination of science, economics, and sociology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup> In 2002 American biologist <a href="/wiki/E._O._Wilson" title="E. O. Wilson">E.O. Wilson</a> observed that:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:03_118-2"><a href="#cite_note-:03-118">[117]</a></sup> <small>(<a href="/wiki/Emphasis_(typography)" title="Emphasis (typography)">emphasis added</a>)</small>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The problem before us is how to feed billions of new mouths over the next several decades and save the rest of life at the same time, without being trapped in a Faustian bargain that threatens freedom and security. No one knows the exact solution to this dilemma. The benefit must come from an <b>Evergreen Revolution</b>. The aim of this new thrust is to lift food production well above the level obtained by the Green Revolution of the 1960s, using technology and regulatory policy more advanced and even safer than those now in existence.</p></blockquote>

<li id="cite_note-53"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-53">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1" id="CITEREFChibwanaFisher">Chibwana, Christopher; Fisher, Monica. <a class="external text" href="http://www.ifpri.org/publication/impacts-agricultural-input-subsidies-malawi" rel="nofollow">"The Impacts of Agricultural Input Subsidies in Malawi"</a>. International Food Policy Research Institute<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">7 October</span> 2016</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=The+Impacts+of+Agricultural+Input+Subsidies+in+Malawi&amp;rft.pub=International+Food+Policy+Research+Institute&amp;rft.aulast=Chibwana&amp;rft.aufirst=Christopher&amp;rft.au=Fisher%2C+Monica&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.ifpri.org%2Fpublication%2Fimpacts-agricultural-input-subsidies-malawi&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AGreen+Revolution"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-54"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-54">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a class="external text" href="http://news.bbc.co.uk/2/hi/business/8363914.stm" rel="nofollow">Malawi Miracle</a> article on the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> website. According to the <a class="external text" href="http://www.wfp.org/countries/Malawi/News/Malawi--P4P-raising-income-for-women-farmers" rel="nofollow">UN website on Malawi</a> the program was highly effective. This website highlights the women farmers program. The claims of success are substantiated by Malawi government claims at <a class="external text" href="http://www.nso.malawi.net/data_on_line/economics/Trade%20on%20NSO%20website/Malawi%202005%20Trade%20Statistics%20Brief_Release.pdf" rel="nofollow">Malawi National Statistics Organization site</a> <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20091113183331/http://www.nso.malawi.net/data_on_line/economics/Trade%20on%20NSO%20website/Malawi%202005%20Trade%20Statistics%20Brief_Release.pdf" rel="nofollow">Archived</a> 13 November 2009 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a>. The international <a href="/wiki/WaterAid" title="WaterAid">WaterAid</a> organisation seems to contradict these facts with its <a class="external text" href="http://www.wateraid.org/international/what_we_do/where_we_work/malawi/3117.asp" rel="nofollow">report on plans from 2005–2010</a>. Similarly, the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Gaming" title="Major League Gaming">Major League Gaming</a> reported that <a class="external text" href="http://www.wto.org/english/tratop_e/tpr_e/tp331_e.htm" rel="nofollow">Malawi had noted problems</a> including lack of transparency and administrative difficulties. This follows with a recent (2010)  <a class="external text" href="http://www.nyasatimes.com/national/malawi-ranks-153-on-un-human-development-index.html" rel="nofollow">Malawi newspaper tells of UN report</a> <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20101108022538/http://www.nyasatimes.com/national/malawi-ranks-153-on-un-human-development-index.html" rel="nofollow">Archived</a> 8 November 2010 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a> with Malawi one of the lowest on the UN list of developing states, confirmed by this <a class="external text" href="http://www.wfp.org/content/malawi-20052006-biennial-report" rel="nofollow">UN World Food Program report</a>. Another <a class="external text" href="http://www.iss.co.za/pubs/ASR/14No4/EHussein.htm" rel="nofollow">report from the Institute for Security Studies</a> <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20120113105320/http://www.iss.co.za/pubs/ASR/14No4/EHussein.htm" rel="nofollow">Archived</a> 13 January 2012 at the <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a> from 2005, showed corruption still prevailing in Malawi at that time.</span>
</li>
